Section Ill - Governance and Reporting

16

16.1

16.2

Treasury Governance and Reporting

Governance

16.1.1

16.1.2

16.1.3

16.1.4

16.1.5

16.1.6

16.1.7

16.1.8

16.1.9

PO Treasury risks are governed through the following structures:

POL Board: Authority to approve policies and approval limits relating to treasury risk
management resides with the Board. Treasury risk management includes but is not
limited to the following: short-term liquidity management, long-term funding, counterparty
risk management, foreign exchange exposure management and interest rate risk
management. The Board will delegate authorities to facilitate the operation of treasury
risk management and the daily operation of the Treasury function.

ARC Committee: Financial risk management policies and approval limits are
recommended to the Board for approval by the ARC Committee.

Risk and Compliance Committee (“RCC”): Financial risk management policies will be
presented to the RCC for noting prior to submission to the ARC.

Treasury Committee: Is part of the Operations Board and meets on a monthly basis to
review the Treasury Report, review financial risks, report on headroom and working
capital, and report on and recommend changes to policy to the ARC Committee as
required. The Treasury Committee is composed of the CFOO, the POL FD, the HoTTI
and Finance Director Financial Services. Other members of the Operations Board may
attend from time-to-time.

FX Currency Hedging Committee: Meets monthly or more frequently as required from
time-to-time to confirm the value of hedges and timescales of hedges in accordance with
the FX risk management policy. The committee is composed of: the Director of Product;
the Finance Director Financial Services and Telecoms; and the Head of Travel.

16.2.1

16.2.2

The Treasury Report will be produced on a monthly basis. The contents of the report will
include analysis of: note and coin inventory and how it is funded; insurance limits in cash
centres; network cash holdings and inward rems; a monthly forecast update, including
variance analysis for the prior period; Facility Headroom and Security Headroom;
balances held in bank accounts; the net NRF Cap position; fx gains and losses;
exposures to interest rate risks; treasury controls; as well as a summary of any project
work currently being undertaken by Treasury.

The Treasury Committee will meet on a monthly basis as part of the Operations Board.
It will review the Treasury Report and consider any other treasury risk management
issues as required and make recommendations to the ARC.

Tab 9.1 Treasury Policy

I - Introduction

Background

This document sets out the risk management framework, policies and authorities adopted by Post
Office Limited (“POL”) and its subsidiaries (together the “Group”) in relation to its treasury
activities and is an update of the paper approved by the ARC Committee in March 2018. It is
recognised that Post Office Management Services Limited (“POMS”) is subject to regulatory and
fiduciary obligations which require derogation from some of the following policies. POMS will
determine where there is a conflict between its obligations and these policies and amendments
will be agreed and documented. A service agreement will set out the treasury activities which will
be carried out on behalf of POMS.

This document should be read in conjunction with the wider Group Delegated Authorities. For
the avoidance of doubt, in the case of inconsistencies the Group Delegated Authorities will prevail.

The treasury risk management framework has been designed to:

protect financial asset values;
minimise income statement volatility;

ensure financial obligations are met as they fall due;

secure long-term funding to meet overall business objectives and shareholder return
requirements;

ensure regulatory obligations are met.

ec eee

The key treasury risks are:

Short-term cash and liquidity risk — the Group does not have sufficient short-term liquidity to
meet payment obligations;

Medium and long-term funding risk — the Group does not have sufficient committed long-term
funding in place to meet business objectives and going concern obligations;

« Counterparty credit risk — a financial institution counterparty cannot meet its obligations to the
Group. Such obligations may arise from: investing the Group’s surplus cash balances (see
investment risk, below); entering into derivatives transactions; entering into committed facility
arrangements; and certain other commercial arrangements with clients.

«Investment risk — arising from investing the Group’s surplus cash balances;

e Foreign exchange risk - arising from holding currency note inventory in branches and cash
centres to meet on-demand requirements from customers;

Interest rate risk — arising from the impact of changes in interest rates on the cost of funding,
the returns earned on the investment of surplus cash, and the returns earned on the POca
cash balances;

« Bank relationship risk — the Group does not manage its bank relationshij
manner;

Commodity price risk — arising from the impact of changes in commodity prices on operational
costs;

e Settlement risk — the risk that operational and business payments are not executed in
accordance with agreed policies and procedures, are not settled in a timely manner or are
exposed to the possibility of fraud;

e Regulatory risk — arising from POL failing to meet its regulatory obligations around its treasury
activities;

Proper recording of treasury transactions, including the reconciliation of bank statement
balances to ledger balances in a timely manner;

* Loss or theft of cash.

in an appropriate

In this document authorities have been delegated to the Chief Financial and Operating Officer
(the “CFOO"), the POL Finance Director (the “POL FD”), and the Head of Treasury, Tax and
Insurance (the “HoTTI”), being the roles and titles existing as at February 2019. Where titles
change over time authorities will rest with those persons performing substantially the same roles.
In any case of doubt confirmation will be provided by the Company Secretary.

2. Policy Overview

21 The Board is averse to treasury risk. The risk management framework and policies have been
designed to reduce risk and concentrate on five principal areas to achieve this:

« Market Risk: to minimise any potential loss due to a change in market factors (e.g. interest
rates, exchange rates or commodity prices);

e Credit Risk: to minimise any potential loss due to a change in the credit-worthiness of a
counterparty;

« Business Risk: to minimise any potential loss due to economic factors;

* Operational Risk: to minimise any potential loss due to system, people, legal and other
external events;

e Regulatory Risk: to minimise the risk that POL fails to meet its regulatory obligations around
treasury activities.
2.2 Day-to-day operation of treasury policy and the activities of the Treasury function are the
responsibility of the HoTTI, who reports to the POL FD. Treasury activities are reported on a
monthly basis to the Treasury Committee, which is part of the Operations Board, for review and
oversight. The composition and responsibilities of the Treasury Committee are set out in section
16.1
2.3. Any proposed amendments to, or derogations from, policy will be considered in the Treasury
Committee and approved by the Audit, Risk and Compliance (“ARC”) Committee or, if
appropriate, by the Board.
2.4 Treasury is responsible for the following activities. These activities will only be undertaken by
Treasury unless an alternative arrangement has been formally approved by the ARC Committee
or the Board:
management of bank account structures to provide automated concentration of cash and/or
offset of balances;

management of the Group’s short-term cash flow forecasting process;

arrangement and management of short-term committed funding;

monitoring the debt capital structure to ensure that the Group has sufficient funding to support
medium and long-term forecast requirements and to minimise refinancing risks;

management of short, medium and long-term borrowing requirements;

e providing input to and critical review of the Group’s medium and long-term cash flow
forecasting process;

« fulfilment of obligations under the rules of the Bank of England's Note Circulation Scheme;

* setting counterparty limits for the financial institutions with which Group does business;

short-term liquidity management and the investment of surplus cash balances;

* executing FX hedges in accordance with the instructions of the FX Committee, using approved
instruments to hedge out to a maximum of 6 weeks;

monitoring net interest rate exposure;

managing bank relationships, in relation to corporate treasury activity;

* monitoring exposure to commodity price volatility;

« executing payments and administrating payments systems;

acting as a centre of excellence in providing guidance and advice on all operational banking,
payments and other treasury-related matters;

e regularly reviewing mandates;

* ensuring adherence to internal controls around internet banking systems and security;

ensuring adherence to treasury-related regulatory obligations.

25 Cash forecasting must be completed in accordance with Treasury's instructions and deadlines
and will support short-term, medium-term and long-term forecasting with the current Strategic
Plan of the Board (currently the 5-year plan to 2020/21). Any material variances are to be
escalated to the POL FD.

26 Compliance with the treasury policies set out in this document is mandatory, subject to the
derogations provided to POMS noted in 1.1 above.

" Detailed Policies for the Management of Financial and Other Risks Relating to Treasury

Key Policies

3. Short-Term Cash and Liquidity Management

Business Context

3.1. Ona daily basis the Group has significant operating, investing and financing cash flows across
its bank accounts, arising in relation to client-related activity across our counters, and as well as
its own business-related activity. Client-related inflows and outflows are material and volatile with
approx. £65 billion of flows each year. Flows can vary significantly depending on the day of the
week and time of year and can also be materially impacted by other factors, out of the Group’s.
control, such as the weather. Even with appropriate long-term committed funding in place there
is therefore a short-term liquidity risk that the Group does not have resources available to meet
its day-to-day payment obligations as they fall due.

Risk Management Objectives

3.2 The objective of the short-term cash and liquidity management policy is to ensure that the Group
has appropriate liquidity in the right place at the right time to meet its payment obligations as they
fall due.

Main Policy Statement

3.3 Through a combination of efficient bank account structures and accurate short-term cash flow
forecasting, together with access to appropriate levels of committed short-term liquidity, Treasury
will ensure that the Group can meet its obligations as they fall due.

Supporting Policy Guidelines
3.4 Bank Account Structures

3.4.1. Where possible, Treasury will manage cash balances within pooling arrangements which
enable cash to be efficiently and effectively concentrated and debit and credit balances
to be offset. Business units are not permitted to operate bank accounts that are outside
these pooling arrangements unless authorised in writing by Treasury.

3.4.2 Delegated Authorities

* Approve addition of bank account to existing pooling arrangement - HoTTI
« Approve removal of bank account from existing pooling arrangement - HoTTI
* Approve creation of new pooling arrangement - POL FD

3.5 Short-term Cash Flow Forecasting

3.5.1 Short-term cash flow forecasting is an essential tool for the Group and enables it to have
confidence that its committed facilities are sufficient to provide the liquidity needed to
meet its day-to-day payment obligations.

3.5.2 Treasury will prepare a short-term, daily rolling forecast of the utilisation of the BEIS
Facility and the NRF. The forecast, by day, covers a period of up to two accounting
periods. Treasury will issue:

daily reporting to the HoTTI analysing variances of same-day and two-day forecasts
to actuals;

* a weekly Liquidity Report to the CFOO and POL FD updating the forecast for the
following week and providing a variance analysis for last week;

 amonthly Forecast Update to the CFOO and POL FD updating the forecast for the
following two periods and providing a variance analysis for the last period.

3.5.3. The forecasts and variances will be reviewed on a daily basis by the HoTTI. Monthly

Treasury Risk Management Framework, Alisdair Cameron Page 5

Forecast Updates will be included in the Treasury Report and reviewed by the Treasury
Committee. The ARC will be updated by exception.

3.6 Committed Short-term Funding

3.6.1 Treasury’s first responsibility is to ensure that sufficient liquidity and facilities are available
to the Group to fund its operations. Funding is therefore negotiated and managed
centrally and the management of individual cash pools will be dealt with by Treasury

3.6.2 Short-term liquidity is managed as follows: POL has access to a £950m working capital
facility provided by the Department of Business, Energy and Industrial Strategy (“BEIS”)
(the “BEIS Facility”). The BEIS Facility is available until March 2021. A utilisation request
must be provided to BEIS two days before drawdown. Forecasting variances may lead
to a shortfall between the amount drawn down and the actual amount required. The
strategy to mitigate the risk of a shortfall between forecast and actual funding
requirements is to hold a liquid investment reserve of £5m (the “Investment Reserve’).
Historically POL has tended to overdraw the BEIS Facility because it did not have access
to an emergency source of short-term funding other than the NRF. Any changes to the
targeted investment reserve will be reported to the Treasury Committee in the monthly
Treasury Report. Treasury can also use a £5m uncommitted overdraft facility with
Barclays, use the NRF (see 3.6.3 below), or use the £50m short-term credit facility
provided by BEIS (the “BEIS Short-term Facility”) (see 3.6.6 below).

3.6.3 In addition, POL is a member of the Bank of England’s Note Circulation Scheme (the
“NCS"). The scheme allows POL to declare and sell eligible notes to the Bank of England
(the “Bank”) overnight with a commitment to buy those notes back from the Bank first
thing the next morning. This reduces the Group’s overnight funding requirement. The
NCS rules require the provision of collateral to the Bank. Collateral is currently provided
on behalf of POL under a Facilities Agreement entered into by POL with National
Westminster Bank Plc! under which the bank makes available: a £400m intra-day facility;
a £350m overnight NRF facility (for the purposes of providing overnight collateral to the
Bank); and, a £1m collateral facility, used in connection with our crime insurance.

3.6.4 The NCS rules also require that POL has a crime insurance in place that is compliant
with BoE requirements.

3.6.5 The amount available to be used under the NRF over the course of the Bank’s financial
year (to October) is constrained by a cap (the “Cap”) that POL generates, mainly as a
function of outward rems processed from its NCS cash centres. Treasury will monitor
utilisation of the NRF against the Cap to ensure that no more than the Cap generated is
used over the course of the year and that financial penalties are therefore avoided. Cap
generation and NRF utilisation will be reported to the Treasury Committee on a monthly
basis via the Treasury Report.

3.6.6 POLhas arranged a £50m short-term credit facility with BEIS. The facility is available on
a same-day basis up to 11:45 am.

3.6.7. Any new borrowings require Board approval. See 4 Medium and Long-term Funding
Requirement.

3.6.8 The delegated authorities for drawdowns are set out in Appendix D and in 3.6.9 below.

3.6.9 Delegated Authorities

Approve change to Investment Reserve (nil to £20m /for up to 2 weeks) - HOTTI
Approve change to Investment Reserve (up to £50m /for more 2 weeks) - CFOO

Approve drawdown - under other external borrowings, including the BEIS Short-term

the event that new subsidiaries are introduced into the Group structure then, provided
such subsidiaries are subsidiaries under the 2006 Companies Act definition, then 3.7 will
also be applicable for loans to/from those subsidiaries.

In 2019 POL is considering a legal entity optimisation project under which certain wholly-
owned subsidiaries of POL will become sister companies of POL under a new holding
company structure. Provided that loans to/from any sister company are permitted under
the BEIS Facility and the entity’s Articles of Association then they will be permitted under
3.7 and will be executed within delegated authorities set out herein.

From time-to-time POL may enter into short-term funding arrangements with First Rate
Exchange Services Limited (“FRES”) under which FRES provides a loan to POL to fund
additional holdings of foreign currency note inventory. Such loans are also permitted
under 3.7 and must be executed within the delegated authorities set out herein.

Tab 9.1 Treasury Policy

4. Medium and Long-term Funding Management
Business Context

41 The Group develops its strategic objectives and prepares long-term business plans to meet those
objectives. Such objectives will include the continued participation in the Bank of England’s Note
Circulation Scheme (the NCS") in order to ensure an adequate supply of notes for the branch
network. The Group must ensure that it has sufficient committed long-term funding in place to
meet these plans. There is a risk that the funding in place is not sufficient to achieve business
objectives or to adequately withstand unforeseen changes to plans.

4.2 In order to present its financial statements on a going concern basis the Group must demonstrate,
on an annual basis at each balance sheet date, that it has sufficient committed funding in place.

4.3. The Group's existing funding arrangements, including the facilities made available to enable
participation in the NCS, are set out in 3. Short-term Cash and Liquidity Management.

Risk Management Objective
4.4 The objective of the medium and long-term funding management policy is to ensure that the

Group has sufficient committed long-term funding in place to meet business objectives and going
concern obligations.

Main Policy Statement
45 Through a combination of accurate medium and long-term cash flow forecasts and the monitoring
of headroom, together with access to appropriate levels of long-term committed funding, the

Group will ensure it has sufficient funding in place to meet business objectives and going concern
obligations.

Supporting Policy Guidelines

46 Medium and Long-term Cash Flow Forecasting

4.6.1 Medium and long-term cash flow forecasting is an essential tool for the Group and
enables it to have confidence that its committed facilities are sufficient to provide the
liquidity needed to meet its business objectives and loan repayments.

4.6.2 Treasury will provide input to Group’s medium and long-term forecasts, in particular the
‘one-year and five-year strategic forecasts and in accordance with the current Board
Strategy.

47 Funding Strategy

4.7.1. The CFOO and the POL FD will recommend to the Board the appropriate debt capital
structure for the Group. The Group will have a debt maturity profile and funding structure
adequate to meet its:

* business objectives, including growth strategy;
* going concern obligations.

4.7.2 The debt capital structure and maturity profile will be monitored by the CFOO and POL
FD, and reviewed by the Treasury Committee to ensure that the Group has appropriate
funding available to support its long-term plans. Where possible, the Group seeks to
minimise its refinancing risk by adopting a range of maturities for its debt facilities.
Maturity of existing facilities will be monitored to ensure that negotiations commence in a
timely manner to extend or replace them.

5.

Counterparty Credit Risk Management

Business Context

5.1

5.2

Counterparty credit risk arises where a financial institution counterparty cannot meet its
obligations to the Group. Due to the nature of POL’s business activities such exposures arise
both as part of POL’s normal corporate treasury activities and its other client-related activities.
Exposures arise primarily as follows:

Corporate Treasury Activity

5.1.1

5.1.2

Investment of Surplus Cash Balances - Total exposure of approximately £5m but may
increase up to £50m when the investment reserve is increased during holiday periods.
(See 6. Investment Risk Management.)

Mark-to-Market of Derivatives - Derivative contracts (including FX swaps, FX forwards
and interest rate swaps) where the mark-to-market position has moved in favour of POL
such that the counterparty owes money to POL under the contract. Exposure arises due
to changes in market rates. Because FX maturities are managed within one month total
exposure is currently minimal.

Committed Facilities - Commitments made by a bank or other funding provider under
facilities that remain undrawn by POL. Such facilities currently comprise: the BEIS
Facility and the BEIS Short-term Facility; and, the £400m intra-day facility / £350m
overnight NRF facility provided by National Westminster Bank Plc. The exposure relating
to the BEIS Facility and the BEIS Short-term Facility is considered to be nil but there is
an exposure on National Westminster Bank Plc that fluctuates during the day depending
on how much is utilised under the facilities. Total exposure may be up to £400m.

Other Client-Related Activity

5.1.4

5.1.6

5.1.7

Banking Framework - Over-the-counter banking transaction services with retail and
business customers. Transactions are cleared through the LINK system with daily
settlement to POL received from Barclays Bank PLC this creates a daily net direct
exposure to Barclays Bank PLC of up to £30m. In addition, POL would also be exposed
to the failure of an individual client bank to meet its obligations under the LINK system.

Debit and Credit Card Processing - When a customer makes a payment to POL over-
the-counter using either a debit card or a credit card settlement is received by POL via
GPUK LLP (“GlobalPay”) on the next business day. This creates a one-day credit
exposure against GlobalPay. Total exposure fluctuates but is approximately £75m.

Cheque Clearing - when a customer makes a payment to POL using a cheque it creates
a short-term exposure (up to two days) exposure against the bank on which the cheque
is drawn. The total exposure on cheques is approximately £25m but this is disaggregated
between the banks on which the cheques are drawn.

Other Client-Related Activity - Exposures arising from other client-related activities.

- ATM Withdrawals — Exposure to Bank of Ireland linked to cash withdrawals from ATMs.
The exposure varies significantly, depending on the time of the year and day of the
week, between £20m and up to £135m.

- POca Related Flows — Exposure to JPMorgan Europe Limited in respect of POca-
related flows across POL counters. Flows between 13:00 on the previous day and
13:00 are aggregated and paid same day. The exposure fluctuates significantly
depending on the day of the week and time of the year and is impacted by holiday
periods and winter fuel payments. It can vary between £20m and up to £125m.

This policy focuses on counterparty credit risk arising from POL’s corporate treasury activities.

Risk Management Objectives

5.3

The objective of the counterparty credit risk management policy is to minimise the Group’s risk of
loss in its corporate treasury activities as a result of the failure of a financial institution
counterparty.

Main Policy Statement

5.4

Treasury will minimise the risk of loss due to the failure of a financial institution counterparty to
meet its obligations by only entering into corporate treasury transactions with highly-rated
counterparties and through credit approvals, limits and monitoring procedures.

Supporting Policy Guidelines

5.5

5.6

5.7

5.8

5.9

5.10

5.11

5.12

Treasury will only enter into corporate treasury transactions with appropriately approved financial
institution counterparties.

The Group's corporate treasury-related credit risk arises primarily from the investment of surplus
cash balances. For the purpose of the investment of surplus cash balances limits are allocated
according to rating band rather than specified counterparty. Approved counterparties and sub-
limits applicable to deposits (as at March 2019) are set out in 6 Investment Risk Management.
Deposit limits will fluctuate with changes to credit ratings.

When monitoring the credit quality of counterparties Treasury will use short-term and long-term
credit ratings from S&P and Fitch. The weaker of the two ratings will be used for decision-making
purposes.

Approved counterparties and credit limits for other transaction types are set out in Appendix A.

New counterparties and limits may be approved from time to time. Treasury will make a
recommendation to the Treasury Committee based on credit ratings for consideration and
recommendation to the ARC.

Exposures to investment counterparties will be monitored separately and reported to the HoTTI
on a daily basis and to the Treasury Committee on a monthly basis in the Treasury Report. See
6. Investment Risk Management. Exposures to corporate treasury counterparty activities will be
aggregated (including investment counterparties) and reported to the Treasury Committee on a
monthly basis together with changes to credit ratings as part of the Treasury Report.

Delegated Authorities

* Approve new financial institution counterparty - ARC
e Approve financial institution counterparty limit - ARC

Note on the Implications of Ring-fencing - Effective 1 January 2019 the major UK banks were
required to implement the Government's ring-fencing requirements. In 2018 the Group’s bank
accounts and the £400m facilities with Royal Bank of Scotland Pic were transferred to National
Westminster Bank Plc as part of the bank’s restructuring to meet these requirements. From 2019
these accounts and facilities will sit inside the ring-fence. (It should be noted that the interest rate
swap executed in April 2018 with NatWest Markets Pic sits outside the ring-fence.) Provided that
the S&P and Fitch long-term and short-term credit ratings of National Westminster Bank Plc (or
any other entity inside or outside the ring-fence) were the same as, or better than, Royal Bank of
Scotland Pic then all references to Royal Bank of Scotland Plc were deemed to apply to National
Westminster Bank Pic (or those other entities). This approach was also applied for Barclays Bank
PLC and Lloyds Bank plc.

6. Investment Risk Management
Business Context

6.1 Treasury manages short-term liquidity to target a cash buffer of £5m. The buffer is reduced to nil
at period ends and can be increased up to £50m around holiday periods when liquidity risks are
highest. This creates surplus cash balances that can be invested by Treasury.

Risk Management Objectives

6.2 The three core objectives of the Group’s investment risk management policy are: (i) security — to
preserve the principal sum; (ii) /iquidity — to ensure investments are accessible when needed; (iii)
yield — to optimise return on investments.

Main Policy Statement

6.3 The Group’s overall consideration when depositing surplus cash balances is the preservation of
the principal sum. Surplus cash balances will be invested by Treasury to optimise return, subject
to counterparty credit risk considerations. These investments will not be subject to fluctuation in
capital values.

Supporting Policy Guidelines

6.4 Permitted Investment Instruments - Treasury are permitted to use the following investment
instruments: bank term deposits and deposits on interest-bearing accounts; money market funds
(‘MMFs”); and, when appropriate, deposits with the Debt Management Office (“DMO”).

65 Permitted Currencies — Treasury will only invest in £-denominated instruments.

6.6 Approved Bank Counterparties and Deposit Limits - It is the Group’s policy to establish and
monitor limits for each of the counterparties that it makes investments with.

6.6.1 Limits for term deposits and interest-bearing accounts (“deposit limits”) are based on
credit rating bands rather than specific counterparties. Counterparties are allocated to
bands based on the lower of the S&P and Fitch long-term credit rating as follows:

(a)

DAA 120
AA+ to AA- 90
A+ to A- 60
BBB+ 30
BBB and below 0

(1) Based on lower of S&P and Fitch long-term credit rating

6.6.2 Counterparties must have a long-term S&P or Fitch credit rating of at least BBB+ and a
short-term S&P or Fitch credit rating of A2/F2.

6.6.3 Counterparties must also be a member of CHAPS (see Appendix C for a list of CHAPS

banks).

6.8 Money Market Fund Investment Criteria - It is the Group's policy to establish and monitor limits

for each of the MMFs that it invests in.

6.8.1. The MMF must be rated by at least one of S&P and Fitch. If rated it must be rated AAAm
by S&P and AAAmmf by Fitch
6.8.2 POL’s holding as a proportion of the fund size must not be greater than 10%.
6.8.3. MMFs must have a constant net asset value (CNAV) (also referred to as stable NAV) or
a Variable Net Asset value (VNAV) (also referred to as accumulating NAV).
6.8.4 MMFs must have daily liquidity.
6.8.5 Investment is limited to £50m in any one MMF.
6.8.6 Investment in Prime Liquidity Funds is limited to £350m
6.8.7 Investment in Government Funds is limited to £150m.
6.8.9 Where a single provider has segregated Prime Liquidity Funds and Government Funds,
investments can be made in both MMFs subject to the limits above.

6.13 Limit Breaches

6.13.1 When Treasury are aware of a potential breach in advance (for example, when Treasury
choose to hold in excess of the authorised limit because no other investments
opportunities are available) approval must be obtained from either the CFOO or the POL
FD for a temporary increase to the limit. The temporary increase will normally be for no

longer than one night.

6.13.2 When Treasury are not aware of the breach in advance (for example, where we receive
more cash into our Barclays accounts than we had forecasted) Treasury will notify the
CFOO of the breach immediately on becoming aware of it but in any event no later than

close of business on the day after the breach occurred.

7 Foreign Exchange Exposure Management
Business Context

71 Foreign exchange risk principally arises from holding foreign currency note inventory in branches
and cash centres to meet “on demand” requirements from customers. All currencies are
purchased from FRES. The exchange risk arises from the time of purchase from FRES to the
sale of currency to the customer. The size of balances on hand is determined by demand. POL
holds note inventory balances in approximately 70 currencies. On average, currency holdings
are c. £60m but can peak at over £100m during holiday periods.

Risk Management Objectives

7.2 The objective of the foreign exchange exposure management policy is to minimise the impact on
the Group's income statement of foreign currency exposures arising from its day-to-day
operations.

Main Policy Statement

7.3 Through a combination of periodic monitoring of foreign exchange exposures and entering into
hedges within approved hedging bands the Group will ensure its exposure to fluctuations in
exchange rates is minimised.

Supporting Policy Guidelines

74 The Head of Travel Money analyses the report of foreign currency note holdings in the network
which is prepared by Supply Chain and the daily reports of foreign currency holdings provided by
Treasury.

7.5 Amonthly meeting of the FX Committee is held, attended by: the Director of Product; the Finance
Director Financial Services and Telecoms; and the Head of Travel. The meeting is held to confirm
the value of hedges and timescales of hedges in accordance with the FX risk management policy
outlined below.

76 Detailed foreign exchange risk management policy statements

7.6.1 EUR and USD holdings will be hedged 100%; currencies with exposures over £1.5m will
be hedged 90% to 100%; other currencies with exposures over £1 million will be hedged
70%.

7.6.2 Atleast 80% and no more than 120% of qualifying exposures will be hedged based on
the average of (1) the previous period’s actual holdings and (2) the forecast for one month
forward.

7.6.3 Hedges will be closed out and reset to periods between two weeks and five weeks.
Longer-dated hedges will be set to mature at a monthend and will be revalued at each
intervening month end based upon the mark-to-market valuation provided by the hedging
bank.

7.6.4 Hedging will be conducted with counterparties approved by the Treasury Committee (see
5 Counterparty Credit Risk Management)

7.6.5 Trades will be executed at a pre-arranged margin with all counterparties.

7.6.6 The maturity of financial instruments used to hedge foreign exchange exposures will
normally be about a month but can be no longer than six weeks.

7.6.7 Permitted Instruments - Foreign currency exposures can only be hedged using foreign
currency outright forwards or swaps.

7.6.8 FX hedging instruments can only be used to hedge exposures generated by holding
currencies to meet on-demand transactions by customers.

8

Interest Rate Exposure Management

Business Context

81

8.2

The Group is exposed to changes in interest rates via its Libor-linked funding and the returns it
earns on cash balances. Increases in interest rates will increase the Group’s cost of funding and
increase the return it earns on cash, mainly linked to Post Office card account (“POca”) balances.

The Group's funding is via the BEIS Facility maturing in 2021 and the NRF. Interest rates on both
facilities are linked to Libor. POL also earns commission (credited to revenue) on the balances
of benefit payments held by JP Morgan, the POca cash balances. The commission interest
received is also linked to Libor. The interest receivable on the POca cash balances has
historically exceeded the interest payable on POL’s borrowings and is expected to do so for the
foreseeable future, despite the long-term decline of POca cash balances. The interest payable
on POL’s funding is a natural hedge of the commission interest receivable.

Risk Management Objectives

8.3

The objective of the interest rate risk management policy is to minimise exposures to income
statement impacts of changes in interest rates.

Main Policy Statement

8.4

The Group will monitor its exposures to changes in interest rates on a regular basis and
recommend hedging strategies, if appropriate.

Supporting Policy Guidelines

8.5 Treasury will obtain forecasts of interest payable / commission receivable and the net interest
rate exposure will be monitored by Treasury and, if appropriate, a proposal to hedge the exposure
will be put to the Treasury Committee prior to approval by the Board.

8.6 The suitability and effectiveness of the interest rate risk management policy will be reviewed at
each Treasury Committee meeting. Any proposed changes will be reported to the ARC
Committee for approval and submission to the Board.

87 Permitted Instruments - Hedging will be by way of interest rate swaps. Other instruments may
be approved by the ARC on a case-by-case basis.

8.8 The Government's Managing Public Money Guidelines allow organisations to consider the use of
derivatives but require them to consider their use carefully especially to assess value for money.
The Guidelines require POL to consult its sponsoring department / HM Treasury before executing
any derivative for the first time.

9.

Bank Relationship Management

Business Context

9.1

9.2

Good long-term relationships with banks are crucial to the success of the Group around its
corporate treasury activities. The Group requires support from banks across all its treasury
activities and this support is particularly important for the provision of: short-term liquidity,
including operational overdrafts; credit facilities to enable continued participation in the Note
Circulation Scheme; and, FX instruments and other derivatives, requiring credit to be extended.

Due to the UK-focused nature of the Group, the limited requirement for external funding and a
small amount of ancillary treasury business, the Group has historically focussed on building
relationships with a small group of UK clearing banks.

Risk Management Objective

9.3

The objective of the bank relationship management policy is to establish, maintain and develop
efficient and effective banking relationships with a core group of banks to provide the Group with
long-term banking support irrespective of short-term business conditions and financial market
turbulence.

Main Policy Statement

9.4

The Group will seek to build long-term relationships with two to three of the UK clearing banks.

Supporting Policy Guidelines

9.5

9.6

9.7

9.8

9.9

It is the Group’s policy to build long-term relationships with providers of banking services and
facilities in order to maximise mutual advantage. In allocating new business opportunities,
preference will generally be given to banks where a relationship already exists, but this does not
preclude the use of other banks identified by Treasury should it be appropriate. Any new
relationships will be reported to the Treasury Committee in the monthly Treasury Report for
approval.

Current counterparty relationships, including banks, are listed in Appendix B.

Management of the Group’s bank relationships is the responsibility of the HoTTI and the Chief
Financial and Operations Officer (“CFOO”). Bank selection will be determined by a number of
factors, including service, price, product range, geographic spread and willingness to provide
services. The decision to develop a new relationship will rest with the Treasury Committee.

From time to time POL may require that banking partners enter into Non-Disclosure Agreements.
(‘NDAs’) to protect Group-sensitive information. Approval will be required by the CFOO.

Delegated Authorities

e Approve entering into relationship with new bank - Treasury Committee

e Approve entering into relationship with new bank (prior to Treasury Committee approval) -
CFOO

* Approve entering into NDA with bank - CFOO

10 Commodity Price Exposure Management
Business Context

10.1 The Group is exposed to movements in the price of diesel, gas and electricity used throughout
the business.

Risk Management Objectives

10.2 The objective of the commodity price exposure management policy is to minimise income
statement volatility due to changes in commodity prices.

Main Policy Statement

10.3 Treasury will monitor exposures to these commodities and forecast price movements and may
recommend hedging action to the Treasury Committee or directly to the CFOO to protect the
Group from adverse price movements.

Supporting Policy Guidelines

10.4 The CFOO is authorised to hedge each commodity, where it is believed to be economic to do so,
up to a maximum of 3 years based on forecast future usage.

10.5 Permitted Instruments - permitted hedging instruments are spot purchases, currency deposits,
forward contracts, call options, matched options (e.g. cylinders) and swaps. Futures will not be
used without specific authority of the CFOO.

10.6 The Group will designate commodity cash flow hedges against forecast underlying exposures.
Unrealised gains and losses on hedges will be deferred in reserves. This will be recycled to the
income statement when the hedge matures to match forecast expenditure.

10.7 The suitability and effectiveness of the commodity price exposure management policy will be
reviewed at each Treasury Committee meeting. Any proposed changes will be reported to the
ARC Committee for approval and submission to the Board.

10.8 Delegated Authorities
«Execute commodity price hedges within policy - Treasury

« Approve new commodity price hedge counterparty - CFOO

Other Guidelines

41. Operational Banking
11.1 Bank Facilities
11.1.1 Treasury is responsible for the negotiation of all operational banking facilities and any
changes to existing operational facilities. Such facilities include overdrafts, fx lines, BACS.
limits, intra-day limits and any similar arrangements. Directorates do not have the
authority to negotiate or commit to any new operational banking facilities without prior
approval from Treasury and are not authorised to undertake any discussions regarding
credit lines.
11.1.2 All changes to existing operational banking facilities or any new operational banking
facilities must be agreed by the CFOO.
11.2 Interest and Bank Charges
11.2.1 Bank transaction charges will be negotiated by Treasury to ensure minimum cost to the
Group. Charges incurred will be reviewed by Treasury to ensure that the activity levels
and unit costs applied by the banks to calculate charges are in accordance with agreed
tariffs. Errors are to be notified directly to the bank.
11.3. Bank Accounts
11.3.1 It is the Group’s policy to minimise the number of bank accounts it operates. Treasury
will conduct a bi-annual audit to ensure it has an accurate record of bank accounts.
Accounts not being utilised should be closed. This will be reconciled back to internal and
bank records.
11.3.2 All new bank accounts will be approved by the HoTTI
11.3.3 Where possible all accounts should be within a cash pooling arrangement. It is
recognised that certain constraints apply to POMS cash, where restrictions may preclude
pooling.
11.4 Bank Mandates
11.4.1 Itis the Group’s policy to standardise bank mandates wherever possible. Treasury will
manage and administer all bank mandates centrally. Each bank account must be
supported by a written, up-to-date mandate which is checked against a list of those
colleagues leaving the business on a monthly basis.
11.4.2 Authority levels relating to internet banking systems will be documented separately.
11.4.3 Sole signatory on a bank account is not permitted except for cheques where one
signatory may sign for amounts of up to £50,000.
11.5 Reconciliations
11.5.1 The Financial Accounting & Governance Manager is responsible for bank reconciliations.
11.5.2 The reconciliation process around certain bank accounts has been assigned to Treasury.
For those accounts, Treasury will ensure that all bank accounts are reconciled to the
underlying accounting records and all reconciling items are identified and cleared as
appropriate, in a timely manner.
11.5.3. The HoTTI will ensure that all Treasury-owned reconciliations have been properly carried
‘out and provided to the relevant staff members reporting to the POL FD in accordance
with prescribed deadlines.

12 Payments
12.1 I Manual Payments

12.1.1 Signing mandates are managed by Treasury and must be in place with a bank for any
account on which cheques or similar manual payment instructions (e.g. direct debit
mandates) are issued.

12.1.2 Cheques or other manual payment instructions up to £50,000 may be signed by one
signatory. Cheques or other manual payment instructions greater than £50,000 must be
signed by two signatories.

12.1.3 It is the responsibility of the paying department to ensure that there is adequate
segregation of duties with regard to the preparation of manual payment instructions and
cheques and that written procedures governing the processing of payments are in place.

12.1.4 Cheque books should be kept in a secure place.

12.1.5 Paying-in books should also be kept in a secure place. To prevent credits being made
to unauthorised accounts, only pre-printed paying-in slips should be used when paying
in cheques.

12.1.6 Delegated Authorities
« Sign manual payment instruction - < £50k - Any 1 member of Banking

Authorisation Panel
Sign manual payment instruction - > £50k - Any 2 members of Banking
Authorisation Panel
12.2 I Computer-Generated Cheque Payments

12.2.1. There should be adequate physical security over the hardware and software used for the
preparation of computer-generated cheques. Detailed records should be kept of cheque
stationery utilised and any missing cheque numbers investigated. A monetary limit
should be set for the maximum value of any computer-generated or machine-signed
cheque.

12.3. Manually-Instructed Payments

12.3.1. Where any use is made of electronic payment systems via a bank, staff must ensure that
adequate written control procedures exist to ensure that the bank will only respond to
verified requests from authorised personnel, these include:

e the use of code words;

*  answer-back arrangements with the bank calling back to an authorised signatory
(other than an authorised signatory who has signed the request);

* requests by telephone for transfers to be supported by a written request, signed in
accordance with the mandate, received by the bank prior to dispatch of funds;

«transfer requests should only be sent on company headed notepaper, or pre-printed
forms unique to the Group.

12.3.2 Treasury must approve any proposal to start using an internet banking platform and
undertake a detailed security review.

12.3.3 Ifa bank requests any Group employee to sign an indemnity giving protection to the bank
in respect of payment instructions actioned by the bank, then this document must be
forwarded to Treasury for review and approval prior to signature.

Electronic Transfers

12.41

12.4.7

Electronic Funds Transfer (BACS/CHAPS/Faster Payments) is the preferred means of
payment. Where internet banking systems are used to make such payments, care must
be taken to ensure that there is adequate physical security over the system to prevent
unauthorised access. The networking of internet banking systems should be approved
collectively by the Treasury and IT departments.

Itis the responsibility of Treasury to ensure that there is adequate segregation of duties
in relation to initiating, authorising and releasing payments.

The authorisation process must be fully documented. Non-compliance with the agreed
authorisation procedures will be referred to the CFOO and ARC Committee and is
considered a serious breach of control.

BACS limits will be negotiated with the bank by Treasury and will be communicated to
the relevant business unit. Any request for an increase to a BACS limit must be made
by Treasury.

‘Any recommendations by a bank providing an internet banking system with regard to the
control environment surrounding that system must be adhered to in all respects.

Treasury must approve any proposal to start using internet banking systems or other
host-to-host solutions to initiate payments and ensure that a security review has been
undertaken if appropriate.

Guarantees and Indemnities / Group Support

POL Support for Subsidiaries

13.1.1

13.1.2

13.1.3

13.1.4

13.1.5

POL may be asked to provide a letter of comfort, a letter of awareness or a direct
guarantee or indemnity to a third party to support the activity of its subsidiaries*. Although
a guarantee creates a contingent liability on POL it does not increase the overall liabilities
of the Group. Itis considered reasonable to meet such requests on behalf of a subsidiary.

Requests of this type will be reviewed on a case-by-case basis and POL will also consider
whether it is more appropriate to issue a letter of comfort or letter of awareness.
Generally such a guarantee will not have a cost for POL. The authority to approve and
sign a direct guarantee to a commercial third-party for the benefit of any subsidiary must
be approved in accordance with the Group Delegated Authorities around indemnities.

For the avoidance of doubt 13.1 does not apply to guarantees provided by POL in favour
of subsidiaries in connection with the raising of third-party finance by subsidiaries. All
such guarantees must be considered by the Board.

Delegated Authorities

* Approve and execute a direct guarantee or indemnity to a commercial third party for
the benefit of a subsidiary - See Group Delegated Authorities for Indemnities

As of March 2019 POMS and Payzone Bill Payments Limited are the only subsidiaries of
POL. In the event that new subsidiaries are introduced into the Group structure then,
provided such entities are considered to be subsidiaries under 2006 Companies Act, then
13.1 will also be applicable for guarantees or indemnities for the benefit of those
subsidiaries.

13.2.1

13.2.2

POL may provide a counter-guarantee to a bank to support a guarantee made by that
bank to a third party (a “bank guarantee”) on behalf of POL. Such a bank guarantee may
be used to support financing provided by a third party or to support a commercial
arrangement. Such an arrangement may create a contingent financial exposure for the
Group.

To Support Financing - Where the bank guarantee is used to support a financing
arrangement approval will be by the POL Board

To Support Commercial Activity - Where the bank guarantee is being provided to support
‘commercial activity the authority to approve and sign the guarantee to the bank must be
approved in accordance with the Group Delegated Authorities around indemnities.

do not create a contingent liability of the Group.

Requests will be considered on a case-by-case basis and will require POL Board

14 Regulatory Obligations
14.2 European Market Infrastructure Regulation (“EMIR")
14.2.1 Effective from January 2018, as a result of the changes introduced by MiFID Il, the
Group’s derivative activity is subject to the requirements of EMIR.
14.2.2 POLis classified as a Non-Financial Counterparty “-“ (an “NFC —*)
14.2.3 As an NFC - EMIR places certain obligations on POL, namely:
a) Reporting Obligations - POL must report its derivative contracts to a trade repository
no later than the working day after execution.
b) Risk Mitigation Techniques — POL must: (i) confirm trades in a timely manner; (ii)
have dispute resolution processes in place; and (iii) engage in portfolio reconciliation
14.2.4 POL will delegate reporting to its counterparty in derivatives transactions and will only
execute derivative transactions with counterparties with which it has the appropriate
delegated trade reporting agreements in place.
14.2.5 All trades will be confirmed by the end of the second day after execution.
14.2.6 POL will have ISDA agreements in place with all derivative counterparties to ensure that
dispute resolution and portfolio reconciliation processes are documented.

15.2

15.3

15.4

15.4

ISDA Master Agreements

POL enters into ISDA* Master Agreements with potential derivative counterparties. The ISDA is
an industry-standard agreement which governs the relationship between derivative
counterparties and each transaction entered into under the ISDA. The key provisions of the ISDA
include terms relating to payment and delivery obligations, termination rights, the close-out netting
of transactions on termination, and representation and warranties. When executing derivative
transactions POL enters into confirmations pursuant to the ISDA, which contain the economic
terms of each transaction.

POL will only enter into derivative transactions with counterparties with which it has an ISDA
agreement in place. POL will ensure that ISDA agreements are broadly similar in all material
respects across counterparties. It is policy to standardise ISDAs where possible.

Only Treasury can negotiate ISDAs on behalf of POL.

Delegated Authorities

« Agree changes to an ISDA Schedule - HoTTI
° Approve and execute ISDA agreement on behalf of POL - CFOO

* ISDA — International Swaps and Derivatives Association

Section Ill - Governance and Reporting

16

Treasury Governance and Reporting

Governance

16.1.1

16.1.2

16.1.3

16.1.4

16.1.5

16.1.6

16.1.7

16.1.8

16.1.9

PO Treasury risks are governed through the following structures:

POL Board: Authority to approve policies and approval limits relating to treasury risk
management resides with the Board. Treasury risk management includes but is not
limited to the following: short-term liquidity management, long-term funding, counterparty
risk management, foreign exchange exposure management and interest rate risk
management. The Board will delegate authorities to facilitate the operation of treasury
risk management and the daily operation of the Treasury function.

ARC Committee: Financial risk management policies and approval limits are
recommended to the Board for approval by the ARC Committee.

Risk and Compliance Committee (“RCC”): Financial risk management policies will be
presented to the RCC for noting prior to submission to the ARC.

Treasury Committee: Is part of the Operations Board and meets on a monthly basis to
review the Treasury Report, review financial risks, report on headroom and working
capital, and report on and recommend changes to policy to the ARC Committee as
required. The Treasury Committee is composed of the CFOO, the POL FD, the HoTTI
and Finance Director Financial Services. Other members of the Operations Board may
attend from time-to-time.

FX Currency Hedging Committee: Meets monthly or more frequently as required from
time-to-time to confirm the value of hedges and timescales of hedges in accordance with
the FX risk management policy. The committee is composed of: the Director of Product;
the Finance Director Financial Services and Telecoms; and the Head of Travel.

The Board has delegated the following specific authorities to the CFOO and POL FD.

CFOO: e Approval of investment instrument limits
* Approval of counterparty selection criteria
Approval of counterparties
.

Approval of counterparty limits

POL FD:

Approval of counterparties
e Approval of counterparty limits (within approved
investment instrument limits)

The daily operation of treasury activity is delegated to the panels as shown on Appendix
D. Inall cases members of these panels will be appointed by the Treasury Committee.

Authority levels for write-offs are shown in Appendix F.

Treasury Management Reporting

16.2.1

16.2.2

The Treasury Report will be produced on a monthly basis. The contents of the report will
include analysis of: note and coin inventory and how it is funded; insurance limits in cash
centres; network cash holdings and inward rems; a monthly forecast update, including
variance analysis for the prior period; Facility Headroom and Security Headroom;
balances held in bank accounts; the net NRF Cap position; fx gains and losses;
exposures to interest rate risks; treasury controls; as well as a summary of any project
work currently being undertaken by Treasury.

The Treasury Committee will meet on a monthly basis as part of the Operations Board.
It will review the Treasury Report and consider any other treasury risk management
issues as required and make recommendations to the ARC.
